    $(document).ready(function() {
 				
 				$('#gn-menu').on('click', 'li:has(.tax-drop)', function(e) {
 					if ( (!$(e.target).is('#gn-menu > li')) && (!$(e.target).is('#gn-menu > li > a')) && (!$(e.target).is('#gn-menu > li > a > i')) ) { return; }
 					
 					e.preventDefault();
 					var drop = $(this).children('.tax-drop');
 					
 					if (drop.hasClass('open')) {
 					
 						drop.removeClass('open');
 					} else {
 						$('#gn-menu').find('.tax-drop.open').each(function() {
 							$(this).removeClass('open');
 						});
 						
 						drop.addClass('open');
 					}
 				});
 			});
   </script>

             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/minnesota-associate-dean-tells-the-story-behind-the-media-coverage-of-the-law-schools-budget-challen.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Minnesota Associate Dean Tells The Story Behind The Media Coverage Of The Law School's Budget Challenges&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/minnesota-associate-dean-tells-the-story-behind-the-media-coverage-of-the-law-schools-budget-challen.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b4c66200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Minnesota Logo" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b4c66200b img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b4c66200b-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Minnesota Logo"/>
           </a>
           In response to yesterday's post,
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-of-minnesota-approves-1-year-36-million-subsidy-for-law-school-one-regent-urges-school-to.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            University Of Minnesota Approves $3.6 Million Subsidy For Law School; Regent Urges School To Drop Quest To Retain Top 20 Ranking Due To Projected $100 Million 10-Year Subsidy
           </a>
           , incoming Minnesota Associate Dean
           <a href="https://www.law.umn.edu/profiles/william-mcgeveran" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Bill McGeveran
           </a>
           requested that I post this response:
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           While there have been challenges here at Minnesota, readers should know that the recent media coverage you cite doesn't include the whole story.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           First, of the 11 public law schools in the top 30, the only ones to get a lower percentage of their revenue from state support are Berkeley, Michigan, and Virginia — all with endowments 2 to 4 times larger than ours. The so-called "subsidy" is actually bringing us into line with our peers.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/minnesota-associate-dean-tells-the-story-behind-the-media-coverage-of-the-law-schools-budget-challen.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 23, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/legal-education/">
            Legal Education
           </a>

          </p>

         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b4c30200b">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-irs-scandal-day-1869-in-meeting-with-lois-lerner-mccain-staffer-requested-financially-ruinous-au.html">
           <strong>
            The IRS Scandal, Day 1869:
            <em>
             In Meeting With Lois Lerner, McCain Staffer Requested 'Financially Ruinous' Audits Of Advocacy Groups
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-irs-scandal-day-1869-in-meeting-with-lois-lerner-mccain-staffer-requested-financially-ruinous-au.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-irs-scandal-day-1869-in-meeting-with-lois-lerner-mccain-staffer-requested-financially-ruinous-au.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;The IRS Scandal, Day 1869: &lt;em&gt; In Meeting With Lois Lerner, McCain Staffer Requested 'Financially Ruinous' Audits Of Advocacy Groups&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-irs-scandal-day-1869-in-meeting-with-lois-lerner-mccain-staffer-requested-financially-ruinous-au.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-irs-scandal-day-1869-in-meeting-with-lois-lerner-mccain-staffer-requested-financially-ruinous-au.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;The IRS Scandal, Day 1869: &lt;em&gt; In Meeting With Lois Lerner, McCain Staffer Requested 'Financially Ruinous' Audits Of Advocacy Groups&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-irs-scandal-day-1869-in-meeting-with-lois-lerner-mccain-staffer-requested-financially-ruinous-au.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef0224df31ff60200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="IRS Logo 2" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef0224df31ff60200b img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef0224df31ff60200b-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="IRS Logo 2"/>
           </a>
           Washington Times,
           <a href="https://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2018/jun/22/mccains-office-urged-irs-use-audits-weapons-destro/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            McCain's Office Urged IRS to Use Audits as Weapons to Destroy Political Advocacy Groups
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           A new
           <a href="https://www.judicialwatch.org/press-room/press-releases/judicial-watch-obtains-irs-documents-revealing-mccains-subcommittee-staff-director-urged-irs-to-engage-in-financially-ruinous-targeting/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            report
           </a>
           from Judicial Watch reveals a concerted effort from Sen. John McCain’s office to urge the IRS under Lois Lerner to strike out against political advocacy groups, including tea party organizations.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Thanks to the results of an extensive Freedom of Information Act (FOIA) request that has been delayed for many years, Judicial Watch has obtained several key emails from 2013 that chronicle McCain’s and Democrat Sen. Carl Levin’s efforts to reign in the advocacy groups that sprouted immediately following the Citizens United decision from the Supreme Court.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The documents uncovered by Judicial Watch include notes from a high-level meeting on April 30, 2013 between powerful members of McCain’s and Levin’s staffs and Lerner, then-director of tax exempt organizations at the IRS under Barack Obama. The notes reveal the suggestions from McCain’s former staff director and chief counsel on the Senate Homeland Security Permanent Subcommittee, Henry Kerner who urges Lerner to use IRS audits on the advocacy groups to financially ruin them:
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           In the full notes of an April 30 meeting, McCain’s high-ranking staffer Kerner recommends harassing non-profit groups until they are unable to continue operating. Kerner tells Lerner, Steve Miller, then chief of staff to IRS commissioner, Nikole Flax, and other IRS officials, “Maybe the solution is to audit so many that it is
           <a href="https://www.judicialwatch.org/document-archive/jw-vs-irs-unredacted-1559-pg-19-29/">
            financially
           </a>
           ruinous.” In response, Lerner responded that “it is her job to oversee it all:”
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           <em>
            Henry Kerner asked how to get to the abuse of organizations claiming section 501 (c)(4) but designed to be primarily political. Lois Lerner said the system works, but not in real time. Henry Kerner noted that these organizations don’t disclose donors. Lois Lerner said that if they don’t meet the requirements, we can come in and revoke, but it doesn’t happen timely. Nan Marks said if the concern is that organizations engaging in this activity don’t disclose donors, then the system doesn’t work. Henry Kerner said that maybe the solution is to audit so many that it is financially ruinous. Nikole noted that we have budget constraints. Elise Bean suggested using the list of organizations that made independent expenditures. Lois Lerner said that it is her job to oversee it all, not just political campaign activity.
           </em>
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Judicial Watch
           <a href="https://www.judicialwatch.org/press-room/press-releases/judicial-watch-irs-documents-reveal-lerner-knew-targeting-criteria-of-nonprofit-groups-might-raise-questions/">
            previously reported
           </a>
           on the 2013 meeting.  Senator McCain
           <a class="extl" href="https://www.mccain.senate.gov/public/index.cfm/press-releases?ID=A7956992-F2AB-4BBD-A9CA-D48E8E8BD8FC">
            then issued a statement
           </a>
           decrying “false reports claiming that his office was somehow involved in IRS targeting of conservative groups.”   The IRS previously blacked out the
           <a href="https://www.judicialwatch.org/document-archive/jw-v-irs-13-01559/">
            notes of the meeting
           </a>
           but Judicial Watch found the notes among subsequent documents released by the agency.
          </p>
          <ul style="text-align: justify;">
           <li>
            American Thinker,
            <a href="https://www.americanthinker.com/blog/2018/06/so_irs_tea_party_persecutor_lois_lerner_had_help_all_along_john_mccain_.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             IRS Tea Party Persecutor Lois Lerner Had Help All Along
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            The Federalist,
            <a href="https://thefederalist.com/2018/06/22/report-mccain-staffer-urged-irs-to-conduct-financially-ruinous-investigations-of-non-profits/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             Report: McCain Staffer Urged IRS To Conduct ‘Financially Ruinous’ Investigations Of Non-Profits
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            PJ Media,
            <a href="https://pjmedia.com/trending/former-top-mccain-staffer-urged-lois-lerner-to-audit-non-profits-until-it-becomes-financially-ruinous/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             Former Top McCain Staffer Urged Lois Lerner to Audit Non-Profits 'Until It Becomes Financially Ruinous'
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            Red State,
            <a href="https://www.redstate.com/streiff/2018/06/22/john-mccains-staff-director-urged-lois-lerner-use-irs-punish-tea-party-groups-now/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             John McCain’s Staff Director Urged Lois Lerner To Use The IRS To Punish Tea Party Groups And Where Is He Now?
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            WND,
            <a href="http://www.wnd.com/2018/06/mccain-staffer-wanted-tea-parties-audited-until-it-was-ruinous/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             McCain Staffer Wanted Tea Parties Audited Until It Was 'Ruinous'
            </a>
           </li>
           <li>
            Zero Hedge,
            <a href="https://www.zerohedge.com/comment/11882613" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             McCain Office Involved In IRS Targeting Scandal; Pushed "Financially Ruinous" Audits Of 501(c) Orgs
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           Julie Tarallo, Senator McCain's communications director, calls Judicial Watch's allegations  "outlandish conspiracy theories that are totally contradicted by the facts":
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3557767200c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false">
            <img alt="McCain" border="0" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3557767200c image-full img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3557767200c-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="McCain"/>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
          </p>

         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hamilton-in-london.html">
           <strong>
            <em>
             Hamilton
            </em>
            In London
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>

             <li>

         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           My wife and I are on a 7-day vacation in London, so we of course had to see
           <a href="https://hamiltonmusical.com/london/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Hamilton
           </a>
           .  It was wonderful to see the play with a British audience (King George brought the house down), and to pay by far the lowest price (£200 ($265)) of our multiple
           <em>
            Hamilton
           </em>
           viewings due to an iron-fisted
           <a href="https://help.ticketmaster.co.uk/hamilton-paperless-ticket-info/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            paperless ticket system
           </a>
           that effectively prohibits resale of tickets.
          </p>
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad35576b2200c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false">
            <img alt="Hamilton" border="0" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad35576b2200c image-full img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad35576b2200c-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" title="Hamilton"/>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           See also New York Times,
           <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2016/10/16/theater/oskar-eustis-public-theater.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            ‘Hamilton’ and Heartache: Living the Unimaginable
           </a>
           (Oct. 13, 2016).  For more on my
           <span style="text-decoration: line-through;">
            obsession with
           </span>
           interest in
           <a href="http://www.hamiltonbroadway.com/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Hamilton
           </a>
           , see
           <a href="https://law.pepperdine.edu/about/dean/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            here
           </a>
           and:
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hamilton-in-london.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">

        <div class="article">
         <p class="small muted">
          Friday, June 22, 2018
         </p>
         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b22c6200b">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/weekly-ssrn-tax-article-review-and-roundup-eyal-cohen-reviews-masons-the-tax-subsidy-war.html">
           <strong>
            Weekly SSRN Tax Article Review And Roundup: Eyal-Cohen Reviews Mason's
            <em>
             The Tax Subsidy War
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Mirit Eyal-Cohen
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/weekly-ssrn-tax-article-review-and-roundup-eyal-cohen-reviews-masons-the-tax-subsidy-war.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/weekly-ssrn-tax-article-review-and-roundup-eyal-cohen-reviews-masons-the-tax-subsidy-war.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Weekly SSRN Tax Article Review And Roundup: Eyal-Cohen Reviews Mason's &lt;em&gt;The Tax Subsidy War&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/weekly-ssrn-tax-article-review-and-roundup-eyal-cohen-reviews-masons-the-tax-subsidy-war.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/weekly-ssrn-tax-article-review-and-roundup-eyal-cohen-reviews-masons-the-tax-subsidy-war.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Weekly SSRN Tax Article Review And Roundup: Eyal-Cohen Reviews Mason's &lt;em&gt;The Tax Subsidy War&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/weekly-ssrn-tax-article-review-and-roundup-eyal-cohen-reviews-masons-the-tax-subsidy-war.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           This week,
           <a href="https://www.law.ua.edu/directory/People/view/Mirit_Eyal-Cohen">
            Mirit Eyal-Cohen
           </a>
           (Alabama) reviews a new article by Ruth Mason (Virgina),
           <a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=3191417" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            The Tax Subsidy War
           </a>
           (June 2018).
          </p>
          <div style="border: 1px solid black; margin: 20px; padding: 10px; background-color: #eee;">
           <p style="text-align: justify;">
            <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef01b8d2dfff64970c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
             <img alt="Mirit-Cohen (2018)" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef01b8d2dfff64970c img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef01b8d2dfff64970c-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Mirit-Cohen (2018)"/>
            </a>
            In her article, Mason discusses European anti-subsidy rules in an era of large-scale tax avoidance by multinationals. This Article is especially timely in light of the recent announcements of the European Commission (EC), the European Union’s (EU) executive body, requiring EU Members States to recover amounts of tax subsidies they provided multinational conglomerates such as Apple, Amazon, Chrislaer-Fiat, Starbucks, and others. In the case of Apple, the EC ordered Ireland to collect from Apple the largest tax deficiency in world history — $14.5 billion (plus interest). Under Europe’s state-aid rules, Member States are prevented from distorting private competition by granting exclusive subsidies to particular firms. The EC concluded that Ireland colluded with, and illegally subsidized, Apple by issuing confidential administrative rulings that significantly relieved Apple from Irish tax. These EC decisions involving U.S. multinationals created much turmoil. U.S. Treasury Department issued a white paper stating that such recoveries would violate tax treaties between the United States and EU Member States. Members of Congress proposed waging a “tax war” urging Treasury to consider imposing retaliatory taxes on the EU. In an unprecedented move, the United States sought to intervene in the upcoming Apple appeal, but the EU courts held that it lacked standing.
           </p>
          </div>
          <p>
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/weekly-ssrn-tax-article-review-and-roundup-eyal-cohen-reviews-masons-the-tax-subsidy-war.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">

         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37b26d7200d">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/facebook-makes-it-rain-for-academics-25000-at-a-time.html">
           <strong>
            <em>
             Facebook Makes It Rain For Academics, $25,000 At A Time
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>

           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">

              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;Facebook Makes It Rain For Academics, $25,000 At A Time&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/facebook-makes-it-rain-for-academics-25000-at-a-time.html">

               </i>
              </a>
             </li>

          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p>
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b0883200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Facebook (2016)" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b0883200b img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b0883200b-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Facebook (2016)"/>
           </a>
           Bloomberg,
           <a href="https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2018-06-14/if-you-re-a-facebook-user-you-re-also-a-research-subject?te=1&amp;nl=dealbook&amp;emc=edit_dk_20180615" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            If You’re A Facebook User, You’re Also a Research Subject
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The professor was incredulous. David Craig had been studying the rise of entertainment on social media for several years when a Facebook Inc. employee he didn’t know emailed him last December, asking about his research. “I thought I was being pumped,” Craig said. The company flew him to Menlo Park and offered him $25,000 to fund his ongoing projects, with no obligation to do anything in return. This was definitely not normal, but after checking with his school, University of Southern California, Craig took the gift. “Hell, yes, it was generous to get an out-off-the-blue offer to support our work, with no strings,” he said. “It’s not all so black and white that they are villains.”
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/facebook-makes-it-rain-for-academics-25000-at-a-time.html#more">

            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>

        <div class="article">
         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37b2687200d">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html">
           <strong>
            Holderness: South Dakota v. Wayfair —
            <em>
             The More Things Change
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Holderness: South Dakota v. Wayfair — &lt;em&gt;The More Things Change&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; &amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Holderness: South Dakota v. Wayfair — &lt;em&gt;The More Things Change&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;  on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b0834200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Holderness (2017)" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b0834200b img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b0834200b-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Holderness (2017)"/>
           </a>
           Following up on yesterday's post,
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/5-4-supreme-court-clears-way-to-collect-sales-tax-from-online-retailers-in-todays-wayfair-decision.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Law Profs Weigh In On Supreme Court's
            <em>
             Wayfair
            </em>
            Decision Clearing The Way For Sales Tax Collections From Out Of State Online Retailers
           </a>
           :  TaxProf Blog op-ed:  South Dakota v. Wayfair:
           <em>
            The More Things Change
           </em>
           , by
           <a href="https://law.richmond.edu/faculty/hholdern/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Hayes Holderness
           </a>
           (Richmond):
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           After the better end of fifty years, the physical presence rule is out. That rule, originally established in the 1967
           <em>
            National Bellas Hess
           </em>
           case, prevented a state from compelling a vendor not physically present in the state to collect the state’s sales and use taxes. Though the Court reaffirmed the physical presence rule in its 1992
           <em>
            Quill
           </em>
           decision (largely on stare decisis grounds), the rule had been constantly derided by commentators, states, and Main Street retailers as failing to achieve the goals of the Commerce Clause and as providing an unfair advantage to mail order and internet vendors. Yesterday, the Supreme Court issued its decision in
           <a href="https://www.supremecourt.gov/opinions/17pdf/17-494_j4el.pdf" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            <em>
             South Dakota v. Wayfair
            </em>
           </a>
           and made clear that those critics had been heard.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 22, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/new_cases/">
            New Cases
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/tax/">
            Tax
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html">
            Permalink
           </a>

           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/holderness-south-dakota-v-wayfair-the-more-things-change-.html#comments">

           </a>
          </p>

         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-of-minnesota-approves-1-year-36-million-subsidy-for-law-school-one-regent-urges-school-to.html">
           <strong>
            University Of Minnesota Approves $3.6 Million Subsidy For Law School; Regent Urges School To Drop Quest To Retain Top 20 Ranking Due To Projected $100 Million 10-Year Subsidy
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-of-minnesota-approves-1-year-36-million-subsidy-for-law-school-one-regent-urges-school-to.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-of-minnesota-approves-1-year-36-million-subsidy-for-law-school-one-regent-urges-school-to.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;University Of Minnesota Approves $3.6 Million Subsidy For Law School; Regent Urges School To Drop Quest To Retain Top 20 Ranking Due To Projected $100 Million 10-Year Subsidy&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-of-minnesota-approves-1-year-36-million-subsidy-for-law-school-one-regent-urges-school-to.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-of-minnesota-approves-1-year-36-million-subsidy-for-law-school-one-regent-urges-school-to.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;University Of Minnesota Approves $3.6 Million Subsidy For Law School; Regent Urges School To Drop Quest To Retain Top 20 Ranking Due To Projected $100 Million 10-Year Subsidy&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-of-minnesota-approves-1-year-36-million-subsidy-for-law-school-one-regent-urges-school-to.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39abf7a200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Minnesota Logo" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39abf7a200b img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39abf7a200b-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Minnesota Logo"/>
           </a>
           Following up on my previous post,
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/05/university-of-minnesota-seeks-increase-in-annual-subsidy-to-12-million-to-maintain-top-20-ranking.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            University Of Minnesota Law School Seeks $3.6 Million Increase In Subsidy To Maintain Top 20 Ranking
           </a>
           :  Minnesota Lawyer,
           <a href="https://minnlawyer.com/2018/06/19/u-of-m-regents-subsidize-law-school-for-another-year/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            U of M Regents Subsidize Law School For Another Year
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The University of Minnesota Board of Regents has approved a funding plan that will subsidize the U of M Law School next year with provisional funding for the subsequent two years.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           On June 8, the regents approved U of M President Eric Kaler’s proposal to provide $3.6 million to cover a projected deficit for fiscal year 2019—a one-time infusion of $1.9 million along with a $1.7-million increase in its annual appropriations. The proposal calls for two subsequent years of subsidies dependent on the provision of satisfactory metrics by the school that will allow the regents to assess performance. The plan’s goal is to both maintain the law school’s high national ranking and eliminate the school’s annual deficits by 2022.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Like most law schools, the U of M has been dealing with steeply declining applications and enrollment since about 2010. Since 2013, the school has been coming to the regents to request subsidies, which have totaled about $17 million since then. Law school Dean Garry W. Jenkins has reported that applications and tuition dollars are now modestly increasing for the first time in years, but that the subsidies are still necessary.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-of-minnesota-approves-1-year-36-million-subsidy-for-law-school-one-regent-urges-school-to.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 22, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/legal-education/">
            Legal Education
           </a>

           </a>
          </p>

         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39b0784200b">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html">
           <strong>
            Avi-Yonah &amp; Mazzoni:
            <em>
             Due Diligence In International Tax Law
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Avi-Yonah &amp; Mazzoni: &lt;em&gt; Due Diligence In International Tax Law&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Avi-Yonah &amp; Mazzoni: &lt;em&gt; Due Diligence In International Tax Law&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           Reuven S. Avi-Yonah (Michigan) &amp; Gianluca Mazzoni (S.J.D. 2018, Michigan),
           <a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=3198495" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Due Diligence in International Tax Law
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The concept of due diligence has been primarily developed in the state context (e.g., investor protection, environmental law), where it has been stated that “[t]he obligation to take preventative measures is one of due diligence, not an absolute guarantee against the occurrence of harm.” In international finance law, the concept is applied to private actors, especially financial institutions. The concept was first developed in the prevention of money laundering (covered elsewhere in this book) but then applied to prevention of tax evasion. In that context, since it would put an unreasonable burden on financial institutions to completely prevent tax evasion, all that is required is due diligence.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 22, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/scholarship/">
            Scholarship
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/tax/">
            Tax
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html">
            Permalink
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/avi-yonah-mazzoni-due-diligence-in-international-tax-law.html#comments">
            Comments (0)
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>

         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/06/12/magazine/why-does-a-creepy-co-worker-keep-getting-a-pass.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            New York Times Ethicist
           </a>
           (Kwame Anthony Appiah (Professor of Philosophy and Law, NYU)):
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           <em>
            Academic publishing in law may be unique in that nearly all scholarly journals are edited by second- and third-year law students, rather than professors or lawyers. Decisions about which articles merit publication are made by students who may be 23 years old and whose only relevant legal experience may consist of having studied law for 20 months or so. Nevertheless, these decisions can affect the way the article and its author are viewed. For example, many law schools brag about their faculty’s prestigious article placements, and such placements can also affect hiring, tenure and salary decisions at law schools.
           </em>
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           <em>
            In recent years, a practice has developed in which authors send their manuscripts to friends on other law faculties and ask them to recommend their paper for publication to the editors of their school’s law journal. Law students understandably feel pressure to defer to the professors who give them grades and who are far more experienced.
           </em>
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/ny-times-ethicist-the-dubious-practice-of-law-profs-of-enlisting-friends-on-other-faculties-to-get-a.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 22, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/legal-education/">
            Legal Education
           </a>
           |

           </a>

           </a>
          </p>

         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/frustrated-faculty-struggle-to-defend-tenure-before-its-too-late.html">
           <strong>
            <em>
             Frustrated Faculty Struggle To Defend Tenure Before It’s Too Late
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>

               </i>
              </a>
             </li>

         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p>
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad35515d0200c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Chronicle" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad35515d0200c img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad35515d0200c-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Chronicle"/>
           </a>
           Chronicle of Higher Education,
           <a href="https://www.chronicle.com/article/Frustrated-Faculty-Struggle-to/243675?key=m1JvRRyygNd0EHj5AaFoOxlSDJLOqFN0ss_gDFkftfHfs5fUXxUCg0UXfZ92G6XYdGVTRElkNHB3VnVqN0VMc1dQdXBaSzRoQzVfcWRwMlVkV1V2d21BUk1WQQ" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Frustrated Faculty Struggle to Defend Tenure Before It’s Too Late
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           [T]he argument that tenure is the essential protection faculty members need to do their jobs is one that an increasing number of professors have felt compelled to make — and almost always to less-than-receptive audiences. In an era where skepticism about higher education runs high and anti-intellectualism thrives in the political discourse, the concept of tenure fuels perceptions that professors are a protected class isolated from the rigors of the real world.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Critics of tenure assert that it’s an antiquated protection, one that can mask, even enable, flagging faculty productivity and that, by default, hinders institutional advancement. Tight budgets make matters worse. Tenure limits flexibility in personnel expenses by locking in the full-time positions that institutions have increasingly cast off to instead hire adjunct faculty who are paid far less than their tenured counterparts. ...
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/frustrated-faculty-struggle-to-defend-tenure-before-its-too-late.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>

         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad39ac177200b">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/rasmussen-lessons-for-academic-leaders-from-modern-restructuring-practice.html">
           <strong>
            Rasmussen:
            <em>
             Lessons For Academic Leaders From Modern Restructuring Practice
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/rasmussen-lessons-for-academic-leaders-from-modern-restructuring-practice.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/rasmussen-lessons-for-academic-leaders-from-modern-restructuring-practice.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Rasmussen: &lt;em&gt; Lessons For Academic Leaders From Modern Restructuring Practice&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/rasmussen-lessons-for-academic-leaders-from-modern-restructuring-practice.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/rasmussen-lessons-for-academic-leaders-from-modern-restructuring-practice.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Rasmussen: &lt;em&gt; Lessons For Academic Leaders From Modern Restructuring Practice&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/rasmussen-lessons-for-academic-leaders-from-modern-restructuring-practice.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           Robert K. Rasmussen (Former Dean, USC),
           <a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=3198833" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Lessons for Academic Leaders from Modern Restructuring Practice
           </a>
           , 92 Am. Bankr. L.J. 233 (2018):
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Financial distress has hit higher education. More and more universities and colleges are facing existential challenges as the competition for a dwindling number of students has put a strain on revenues. Unlike leaders in other industries, the presidents and chancellors of a financially distressed institutions of higher education cannot explore the possibility of a Chapter 11 filing under the Bankruptcy Code to restructure their obligations so that they align better with their revenues. Federal law prohibits Title IV loans — the lifeblood of virtually every university and college — from being made to students who attend a school that is in an insolvency proceeding. Yet academic leaders can take lessons from modern Chapter 11 practice: they can, in advance of financial distress, ensure that their boards of trustees have members who can provide advice to the schools’ leaders as to the difficult choices that they face; they can employ restructuring professionals who have experience in turning around operations without a bankruptcy filing; finally, given that many of these institutions have relatively few creditors, they can attempt to negotiate a restructuring support agreement that would restructure the schools’ debts without a bankruptcy filing.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/rasmussen-lessons-for-academic-leaders-from-modern-restructuring-practice.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 21, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/legal-education/">
            Legal Education
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/scholarship/">
            Scholarship
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/rasmussen-lessons-for-academic-leaders-from-modern-restructuring-practice.html">
            Permalink
           </a>
           |

            Comments (0)
           </a>
          </p>

             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;Why The Treasury Department's Top Lawyer Sold Off His Bitcoin Holdings&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/why-the-treasury-departments-top-lawyer-sold-off-his-bitcoin-holdings.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37ae0ee200d-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Treasury Department (2018)" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37ae0ee200d img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37ae0ee200d-250wi" style="width: 250px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Treasury Department (2018)"/>
           </a>
           Law.com,
           <a href="ttps://www.law.com/2018/06/19/why-treasury-departments-top-lawyer-sold-off-his-bitcoin-holdings/?et=editorial&amp;bu=Law.com&amp;cn=20180620&amp;src=EMC-Email&amp;pt=Morning%20Minute" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Why the Treasury Department's Top Lawyer Sold Off His Bitcoin Holdings
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The U.S. Treasury Department’s top lawyer sold off up to $30,000 worth of bitcoin in December, a month after Secretary Steven Mnuchin said the department was looking “very carefully” into illegal uses of the cryptocurrency, according to financial disclosures.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           <a href="https://at.law.com/qAT9a3?cmp=share_twitter" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Brent McIntosh
           </a>
           , a former
           <a href="https://www.law.com/law-firm-profile?id=297&amp;name=Sullivan-%26-Cromwell-LLP" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Sullivan &amp; Cromwell
           </a>
           partner who was confirmed as Treasury’s general counsel in August, reported two sales of bitcoin in December, valuing each at between $1,000 and $15,000, according to disclosures released by the U.S. Office of Government Ethics. The
           <a href="https://drive.google.com/file/d/1oy3F3uzD8LJHHY-SRkbKzksIxEWGg-11/view" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            sales
           </a>
           came at the end of a year that saw bitcoin’s value skyrocket from about $1,000 to a high of nearly $20,000.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           A Treasury Department spokeswoman said Tuesday that McIntosh sold his bitcoin to avoid potential ethics conflicts after being asked in late November to participate in a review of digital currencies. Ethics officials advised McIntosh that his continued ownership of bitcoin could raise recusal issues in certain instances, the spokeswoman said.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/why-the-treasury-departments-top-lawyer-sold-off-his-bitcoin-holdings.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>

         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37ae047200d">

         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/national-taxpayer-advocate-the-irs-should-provide-more-guidance-to-participants-in-the-sharing-econo.html">
           <strong>
            National Taxpayer Advocate:
            <em>
             The IRS Should Provide More Guidance To Participants In The Sharing Economy
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/national-taxpayer-advocate-the-irs-should-provide-more-guidance-to-participants-in-the-sharing-econo.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/national-taxpayer-advocate-the-irs-should-provide-more-guidance-to-participants-in-the-sharing-econo.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;National Taxpayer Advocate: &lt;em&gt; The IRS Should Provide More Guidance To Participants In The Sharing Economy&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/national-taxpayer-advocate-the-irs-should-provide-more-guidance-to-participants-in-the-sharing-econo.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/national-taxpayer-advocate-the-irs-should-provide-more-guidance-to-participants-in-the-sharing-econo.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;National Taxpayer Advocate: &lt;em&gt; The IRS Should Provide More Guidance To Participants In The Sharing Economy&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/national-taxpayer-advocate-the-irs-should-provide-more-guidance-to-participants-in-the-sharing-econo.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37ae03e200d-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Taxpayer Advocate (2016)" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37ae03e200d img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad37ae03e200d-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Taxpayer Advocate (2016)"/>
           </a>
           ina Olson (National Taxpayer Advocate),
           <a href="https://taxpayeradvocate.irs.gov/news/nta-blog-participants-in-the-sharing-economy-lack-adequate-guidance-from-the-irs#.WyqDoN6rp5g.twitter" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Participants in the Sharing Economy Lack Adequate Guidance From the IRS
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           In my
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/01/national-taxpayer-advocate-delivers-annual-report-to-congress-discusses-tax-reform-implementation-un.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            most recent Annual Report to Congress
           </a>
           , I included the IRS’s efforts to reach out to participants in the sharing economy (also know as the “gig economy”) as a Most Serious Problem. ...
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           These new entrants to the sharing economy will need to spend significant time learning about their tax compliance obligations and devote many hours to recordkeeping. For example, the IRS estimates that it takes taxpayers nearly 40 hours to learn about depreciation methods, keep records, and report the depreciation to the IRS. Yet, according to a recent
           <a href="https://www.nase.org/about-us/Nase_News/2016/05/11/small-biz-survey---69-of-sharing-economy-entrepreneurs-received-zero-tax-guidance" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            survey conducted by NASE
           </a>
           , 69 percent of entrepreneurs who participate in the sharing economy received absolutely no tax guidance from the service coordinators.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The NASE survey results underscore the importance of educating sharing economy participants about certain basic tax obligations (i.e., making required quarterly estimated payments throughout the year to avoid penalties). There is an opportunity to create a culture of tax compliance among participants in the sharing economy from the outset. Establishing the tax compliance norms for this emerging industry in its infancy will assist the IRS as this segment of taxpayers grows.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/national-taxpayer-advocate-the-irs-should-provide-more-guidance-to-participants-in-the-sharing-econo.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>

         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/does-feedback-really-improve-law-student-performance.html">
           <strong>
            <em>
             Does Feedback Really Improve Law Student Performance?
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">

            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>

               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/does-feedback-really-improve-law-student-performance.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;Does Feedback Really Improve Law Student Performance?&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/does-feedback-really-improve-law-student-performance.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/does-feedback-really-improve-law-student-performance.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;Does Feedback Really Improve Law Student Performance?&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/does-feedback-really-improve-law-student-performance.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>

          </div>

         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p>
           National Law Journal,
           <a href="https://www.law.com/2018/06/18/ahead-of-the-curve-feedback-on-feedback/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Feedback on Feedback
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Giving law students more feedback and assessments such as practice exams translate into better grades, right?
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Not so fast. An upcoming edition of the University of Detroit Mercy Law Review takes up the subject of so-called formative reviews, but the authors of two articles reach different conclusions about the ability of professor interaction and feedback to improve student performance [Symposium,
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/symposium-the-impact-of-formative-assessment-emphasizing-outcome-measures-in-legal-education.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            The Impact of Formative Assessment: Emphasizing Outcome Measures in Legal Education
           </a>
           , 94 U. Det. Mercy L. Rev. 387-457 (2017)].
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/does-feedback-really-improve-law-student-performance.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
