             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/google-now-displays-acceptance-cost-and-graduation-data-in-college-searche-results.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/google-now-displays-acceptance-cost-and-graduation-data-in-college-searche-results.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;Google Now Displays Acceptance, Cost And Graduation Data In College Search Results&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/google-now-displays-acceptance-cost-and-graduation-data-in-college-searche-results.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3799e79200d-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Montana" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3799e79200d img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3799e79200d-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Montana"/>
           </a>
           Chronicle of Higher Education,
           <a href="Google%20Wants to Play a Bigger Role in Your College Search. Here’s What You Need to Know." rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Google Wants to Play a Bigger Role in Your College Search. Here’s What You Need to Know.
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Google waded into the college-search process on Tuesday, announcing that it would elevate certain statistics about four-year colleges when people use the ubiquitous search engine to seek out information.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Here’s what that will look like in practice, Google says: Enter “University of Montana” into the search bar, and a prominent result will be a selection of statistics about the institution — its graduation rate and average cost after financial aid, among other things.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           To get those stats, Google will draw from two favorite data troves of higher-ed researchers: the College Scorecard and the Education Department’s Integrated Postsecondary Education Data System, known as Ipeds.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           On a search-by-search basis, the change might seem relatively minor. Searches already amplify information on colleges’ acceptance rates and material drawn from their Wikipedia pages. But Google’s immense power means the shift could have real-world ripple effects for students and the colleges recruiting them.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/google-now-displays-acceptance-cost-and-graduation-data-in-college-searche-results.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 19, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/legal-education/">

           </a>
          </p>

         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/christians-introduction-to-tax-policy-theory.html">
           <strong>
            Christians:
            <em>
             Introduction To Tax Policy Theory
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/christians-introduction-to-tax-policy-theory.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/christians-introduction-to-tax-policy-theory.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Christians: &lt;em&gt; Introduction To Tax Policy Theory&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/christians-introduction-to-tax-policy-theory.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/christians-introduction-to-tax-policy-theory.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Christians: &lt;em&gt; Introduction To Tax Policy Theory&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/christians-introduction-to-tax-policy-theory.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           Allison Christians (McGill),
           <a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=3186791" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Introduction to Tax Policy Theory
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Taxation involves the compulsory transfer of resources among members of society. Tax policy is concerned with how societies carry out taxation. That is a technical and legal question, but it is inescapably a political, social, and cultural one as well. To study tax policy is to engage simultaneously with the existential philosophical foundations of taxation: why and how societies tax. This introduction to tax policy theory presents an overview of tax policy discourse. The goal is to outline a working framework for reflection and analysis to examine the ways in which current assumptions and approaches require further development.
          </p>
          <p>
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/christians-introduction-to-tax-policy-theory.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>

         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-boardrooms-need-reform.html">
           <strong>
            <em>
             University Boardrooms Need Reform
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">

              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-boardrooms-need-reform.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>

             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;University Boardrooms Need Reform&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-boardrooms-need-reform.html">

         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p>
           Following up on my previous posts (links below):  Wall Street Journal op-ed:
           <a href="https://www.wsj.com/articles/university-boardrooms-need-reform-1528652211?emailToken=318ba078e32b663aba4df43352737cefOTTeiPj/q7dpwvJJ7yfbvBT3dg1vGOmvBIYceFkFImHDilMwcAHmaRlrGHVSL32/IFThwT7pggUjEFxbvwvYeA%3D%3D&amp;reflink=article_email_share" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            University Boardrooms Need Reform
           </a>
           , by Paul S. Levy:
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           I recently resigned as a trustee of the University of Pennsylvania and an overseer of its law school to protest the shameful treatment of law professor Amy Wax. Her career-threatening offense was to state that in her experience with black students over 17 years at Penn, few had performed in the top half of their class. Penn Law’s dean, Ted Ruger, declared her in error but refused to provide evidence. For dissenting from politically correct orthodoxy, Mr. Ruger forbade Ms. Wax to teach her much-admired first-year course in civil procedure—for which the university gave her an award in 2015.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/university-boardrooms-need-reform.html#more">

         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html">
           <strong>
            Krugman:
            <em>
             Tax Cuts And Leprechauns
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Krugman: &lt;em&gt; Tax Cuts And Leprechauns&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Krugman: &lt;em&gt; Tax Cuts And Leprechauns&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p>
           New York Times op-ed:
           <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/06/15/opinion/tax-cuts-and-leprechauns-wonkish.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Tax Cuts and Leprechauns (Wonkish)
           </a>
           , by Paul Krugman:
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The political news seems even more horrible than usual today. So to get away from the headlines a bit, I’m going to commit some economics. Specifically, I want to pull together some thoughts — some inspired by Gabriel Zucman’s recent work [
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/tax-havens-blunt-impact-of-corporate-tax-cuts.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Tax Havens Blunt Impact Of Corporate Tax Cuts
           </a>
           ], some of my own — about the case or lack thereof for corporate tax cuts, the centerpiece of the only major legislation enacted under Trump. ...
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           There is no question that multinational corporations like low-tax countries like Ireland, and report earning a lot of their profits in those countries. But does this really reflect large-scale capital movements to those low-tax jurisdictions?
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           No, say
           <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="http://gabriel-zucman.eu/missingprofits/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">
            Gabriel Zucman and co-authors
           </a>
           . They produce strong evidence that most of what we see is basically a statistical illusion: corporations use transfer pricing, allocation of rents on intangible assets, etc. to make profits appear in low-tax countries; but there’s very little real production or employment behind those profits. As Figure 3 shows, tax-haven countries end up showing ridiculously high levels of profits relative to wages, basically because the profits aren’t being earned where they’re being reported.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3997bcd200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false">
            <img a="" activity="" actual="" alt="Krugman" and="" around="" as="" based="" big="" border="0" capital="" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3997bcd200b image-full img-responsive" considerations="" corporate="" corporations="" cuts="" economic="" evidence="" for="" hence="" in="" is="" misinterpretation="" move="" much="" multinational="" not="" of="" on="" profits="" rationale="" reported="" short="" so="" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3997bcd200b-800wi" style="display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" supposed="" tax="" the="" title="Krugman"/>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 18, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/legal-education/">
            Legal Education
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html">
            Permalink
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/strongkrugman-tax-cuts-and-leprechauns.html#comments">

           </a>
          </p>

         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hamilton-and-philosophy.html">
           <strong>
            <em>
             Hamilton And Philosophy
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">

              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hamilton-and-philosophy.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;Hamilton And Philosophy&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hamilton-and-philosophy.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">

              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hamilton-and-philosophy.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;Hamilton And Philosophy&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hamilton-and-philosophy.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3997d1a200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Hamilton" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3997d1a200b img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3997d1a200b-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Hamilton"/>
           </a>
           I gotta get back in the classroom:  Professor
           <a href="https://www.mmm.edu/live/profiles/76-carrie-ann-biondi" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Carrie-Ann Biondi
           </a>
           at Marymount Manhattan College is teaching a course in the fall on
           <a href="https://www.academia.edu/36546376/PHIL_332-01_Hamilton_and_Philosophy_Syllabus_Fall_2018?ends_sutd_reg_path=true" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Hamilton and Philosophy
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Alexander Hamilton not only participated in the American Revolutionary War as George Washington’s right-hand man, but he also introduced revolutionary ideas into American political philosophy before and during the early American republic. Inspired by Ron Chernow’s biography of Hamilton, Lin-Manuel Miranda created a revolution of his own on Broadway with his smash-hit
           <em>
            Hamilton: An American Musical
           </em>
           . In this course, we will explore both the political philosophy of Hamilton and examine various philosophical issues surrounding the creation and reception of Miranda’s
           <em>
            Hamilton
           </em>
           .
          </p>
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           Professor Biondi contributed a chapter (
           <em>
            Legacy and Happiness in Hamilton: An American Musical
           </em>
           ) in the book
           <a href="https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/0812699602/ref=as_li_qf_asin_il_tl?ie=UTF8&amp;tag=lawproblo-20&amp;creative=9325&amp;linkCode=as2&amp;creativeASIN=0812699602&amp;linkId=87a00cbe28d4f353d32b99e2701438fc" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            <em>
             Hamilton and Philosophy
            </em>
           </a>
           (2017):
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           In
           <em>
            Hamilton and Philosophy
           </em>
           , professional thinkers expose, examine, and ponder the deep and controversial implications of this runaway hit Broadway musical.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hamilton-and-philosophy.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 18, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/book_club/">
            Book Club
           </a>

            Legal Education

        <div class="article">
         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3991937200b">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/lesson-from-the-tax-court-where-is-a-retirees-tax-home.html">
           <strong>
            Lesson From The Tax Court:
            <em>
             Where Is A Retiree's Tax Home?
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Bryan Camp
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/lesson-from-the-tax-court-where-is-a-retirees-tax-home.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/lesson-from-the-tax-court-where-is-a-retirees-tax-home.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Lesson From The Tax Court: &lt;em&gt; Where Is A Retiree's Tax Home?&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/lesson-from-the-tax-court-where-is-a-retirees-tax-home.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/lesson-from-the-tax-court-where-is-a-retirees-tax-home.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Lesson From The Tax Court: &lt;em&gt; Where Is A Retiree's Tax Home?&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/lesson-from-the-tax-court-where-is-a-retirees-tax-home.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad379cea9200d-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Tax Court (2017)" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad379cea9200d img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad379cea9200d-250wi" style="width: 236px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Tax Court (2017)"/>
           </a>
           The last couple of weeks have seen Tax Court cases with several interesting lessons. The one I choose today is
           <em>
            <a href="https://www.ustaxcourt.gov/UstcInOp/OpinionViewer.aspx?ID=11660">
             Roger G. Maki and Lilane J. Gervais v. Commissioner
            </a>
           </em>
           , T.C. Summary Op. 2018-30 (June 6, 2018). It teaches a lesson about what constitutes travel “away from home” for purposes of the
           <a href="https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/26/162">
            §162
           </a>
           deduction. I posted a basic lesson (
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2017/10/lesson-from-tax-court-what-is-away-from-home.html">
            here
           </a>
           ) on this issue late last year. The wrinkle in today’s case is that the taxpayer was retired and traveled from his home in the Seattle metro area to a house he had inherited, ostensibly to manage the surrounding land for eventual timber sales. The Tax Court decided the travel was deductible. I question whether that’s the right outcome here — it seems to me this was just a commute — but notice this is just a Summary Opinion. That means it can still teach a lesson, even if it carries no precedential weight.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/lesson-from-the-tax-court-where-is-a-retirees-tax-home.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>

            Bryan Camp

            New Cases
           </a>

         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad353a874200c">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html">
           <strong>
            <em>
             The Problem With Law Schools? They Only Prepare Future Lawyers
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;The Problem With Law Schools? They Only Prepare Future Lawyers&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;The Problem With Law Schools? They Only Prepare Future Lawyers&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p>
           Law.com,
           <a href="https://www.law.com/2018/06/12/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers/?et=editorial&amp;bu=Law.com&amp;cn=20180613&amp;src=EMC-Email&amp;pt=Morning%20Minute" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            The Problem with Law Schools? They Only Prepare Future Lawyers
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Working in today’s legal market requires more skill than just knowing the law, but not all law schools have matched their curriculum to this changing marketplace.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           “If you look at the legal market from the point of view of a law student, that is very far removed from the market you see,” said Jae Um, founder &amp; executive director of  legal market insights company Six Parsecs, at the June 8 “Training the 21st Century Lawyer: Envisioning a Legal Industry Alliance” session of Thomson Reuters’ 2018 Legal Executive Forum in New York.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           Um noted that the current model of education, which trains around “conceptual subject matter expertise,” is outdated, and what law schools need to do is focus more on teaching students how to work in today’s legal market. Such a market is defined by the recent rise of legal operation professionals, knowledge management staff, and e-discovery managers, all of whom play an integral part in law firms. The work of today’s lawyers and legal professionals, therefore, is as much about solving a client’s business and operational needs as it is their legal ones.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           William Henderson, professor of law at Indiana University Maurer School of Law, noted that the rise of these new and different types of law firm positions was proof that the industry had undergone a profound change, even if legal education hasn’t kept up.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           “We don’t change very often. But when we change, we change in an order of magnitude that is fairly large,” he said at the forum. “And I hope legal education is on the brink of creating a different narrative.”
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 18, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/legal-education/">
            Legal Education
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html">
            Permalink
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-problem-with-law-schools-they-only-prepare-future-lawyers.html#comments">
            Comments (4)
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>

        <div class="article">
         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad353f601200c">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hackney-why-the-irs-should-go-after-trump.html">
           <strong>
            Hackney:
            <em>
             Why The IRS Should Go After Trump
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hackney-why-the-irs-should-go-after-trump.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hackney-why-the-irs-should-go-after-trump.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Hackney: &lt;em&gt; Why The IRS Should Go After Trump&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hackney-why-the-irs-should-go-after-trump.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hackney-why-the-irs-should-go-after-trump.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Hackney: &lt;em&gt; Why The IRS Should Go After Trump&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hackney-why-the-irs-should-go-after-trump.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           New York Times op-ed:
           <a href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/06/15/opinion/trump-foundation-new-york-attorney-general.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Why the I.R.S. Should Go After Trump
           </a>
           . by Philip Hackney (LSU;
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/04/phil-hackney-leaves-lsu-for-pittsburgh.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            moving to Pittsburgh
           </a>
           ):
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The New York State attorney general yesterday filed a lawsuit against the Donald J. Trump Foundation and its directors, accusing the charity and the Trump family of violating campaign finance laws, self-dealing and illegal coordination with the presidential campaign. It asks that Mr. Trump pay restitution and be prohibited from leading a nonprofit in New York for 10 years.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           As a former attorney for the chief counsel of the I.R.S. who specialized in nonprofit organizations, I believe Mr. Trump is also criminally liable for his actions. If I were still at the I.R.S., based on the lawsuit, I would make a criminal referral, on charges of tax evasion or false statements on a tax return, or both.
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hackney-why-the-irs-should-go-after-trump.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 18, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/tax/">
            Tax
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/hackney-why-the-irs-should-go-after-trump.html">
            Permalink
           </a>

        <div class="article">
         <p class="small muted">
          Sunday, June 17, 2018
         </p>
         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3799cbd200d">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html">
           <strong>
            Supreme Court Votes 7-2 To Deny Accreditation Of Canada's First Christian Law School, Says LGBT Rights Trump Religious Freedom To Ban Student Sex Outside Of Heterosexual Marriage
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;Supreme Court Votes 7-2 To Deny Accreditation Of Canada's First Christian Law School, Says LGBT Rights Trump Religious Freedom To Ban Student Sex Outside Of Heterosexual Marriage&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;Supreme Court Votes 7-2 To Deny Accreditation Of Canada's First Christian Law School, Says LGBT Rights Trump Religious Freedom To Ban Student Sex Outside Of Heterosexual Marriage&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad353a5e8200c-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="Trinity Western" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad353a5e8200c img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad353a5e8200c-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="Trinity Western"/>
           </a>
           Following up on my previous posts (links below):  Globe and Mail,
           <a href="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/canada/article-supreme-court-upholds-provincial-law-societies-right-to-reject/" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Law Societies Can Deny Accreditation to B.C. Evangelical University’s Law School Graduates: Supreme Court
           </a>
           :
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The Supreme Court has upheld the right of provincial law societies to reject the graduates of a proposed Christian law school over its requirement that students abstain from sex outside of heterosexual marriage [
           <a href="https://scc-csc.lexum.com/scc-csc/scc-csc/en/item/17141/index.do" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Trinity Western University v. Law Society of Upper Canada
           </a>
           ;
           <a href="https://www.christianitytoday.com/news/2018/june/canada-supreme-court-rejects-trinity-western-law-school.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            Trinity Western University v. The Law Society of British Columbia
           </a>
           ].
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           In a highly anticipated contest between religious freedom and equality, most of the court said the limit on religious freedom was a minor one – well short of “forced apostasy,” as five of the judges put it. By comparison, the effects on equality, if the school had been accredited, would have been large enough to threaten the integrity of the legal system, the judges said.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           The court had been asked whether the law societies of British Columbia and Ontario were within their rights when they voted not to give licences to graduates of Trinity Western University’s proposed law school at its campus in Langley, B.C. In a pair of 7-2 rulings, the court said they were.
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           “Limiting access to membership in the legal profession on the basis of personal characteristics, unrelated to merit, is inherently inimical to the integrity of the legal profession,” five of the seven judges in the majority wrote.
          </p>
          <p>
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 17, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/legal-education/">
            Legal Education
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html">
            Permalink
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/supreme-court-votes-7-2-to-deny-accreditation-of-canadas-first-christian-law-school-says-lgbt-rights.html#comments">
            Comments (5)
           </a>
          </p>
         </div>

        <div class="article">
         <a id="a6a00d8341c4eab53ef022ad3799da2200d">
         </a>
         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html">
           <strong>
            <em>
             The Tax Court's Constitutional Home
            </em>
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">
            <i class="icon-share">
            </i>
            Share
           </a>
           <div class="dropdown clearfix">
            <div class="tab-arrow">
            </div>
            <ul class="clearfix">
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html">
               <i class="icon-facebook">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html&amp;text=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;The Tax Court's Constitutional Home&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;&amp;via=SoCalTaxProf">
               <i class="icon-twitter">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="https://plus.google.com/share?url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html">
               <i class="icon-google-plus">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://www.linkedin.com/shareArticle?mini=true&amp;url=http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html">
               <i class="icon-linkedin">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="mailto:?subject=&lt;strong&gt;&lt;em&gt;The Tax Court's Constitutional Home&lt;/em&gt;&lt;/strong&gt; on The Taxprof Blog&amp;body=Check this article out on The Taxprof Blog: http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html">
               <i class="icon-envelope">
               </i>
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           Allen Madison (South Dakota) &amp; Sharyn M. Fisk (California State Polytechnic),
           <a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=3181107" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            The Tax Court's Home
           </a>
           , 157 Tax Notes 1249 (Nov. 27, 2017):
          </p>
          <p style="margin: 15px 0px; padding: 0px; border: 0px none; outline: 0px none; font-size: 14px; vertical-align: baseline; background-color: #ebf0f3; line-height: 20px; color: #363636; font-family: Arial,Helvetica,sans-serif; font-style: normal; font-variant: normal; font-weight: normal; letter-spacing: normal; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0px; text-transform: none; white-space: normal; word-spacing: 0px;">
           This article analyzes issues related to the Tax Court’s constitutional status. Although the issue has been debated for decades, recent litigation has revived the issue. In
           <a href="https://www.ustaxcourt.gov/UstcInOp/OpinionViewer.aspx?ID=11092" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
            <em>
             Battat v. Commissioner
            </em>
           </a>
           , [148 T.C. No. 2 (Feb. 2, 2017),] the primary issue before Tax Court was whether the President’s limited removal power over tax judges violates the Constitution’s separation of powers. In addressing this issue, the Tax Court outlined the background on the Tax Court’s status to show the Tax Court is not in the Executive branch. Further, the
           <em>
            Battat
           </em>
           opinion holds that even though the court exercises judicial power, the Tax Court does not exercise the “judicial power of the United States” reserved for Article III courts. Thus, the President’s limited removal power presents no separation of powers violation. The Tax Court did not reach an ultimate answer as to which branch of the government it resides, but it does provide background showing that it lies outside the Executive branch.
          </p>
          <p>
          </p>
          <p>
           <a class="btn btn-small" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html#more">
            Continue reading
            <i class="icon-double-angle-right">
            </i>
           </a>
          </p>
          <p class="posted">
           June 17, 2018 in
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/new_cases/">
            New Cases
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/tax/">
            Tax
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html">
            Permalink
           </a>
           |
           <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-tax-courts-constitutional-home.html#comments">
            Comments (0)
           </a>
          </p>

           <li>
            Chronicle of Higher Education,
            <a href="https://www.chronicle.com/article/An-Ultra-Selective-University/243678?cid=db&amp;elqTrackId=f9d9811b0e8a4e53af57d6ffb303f168&amp;elq=1d747e03527248698c296beaf239c52c&amp;elqaid=19458&amp;elqat=1&amp;elqCampaignId=8907" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">

            <a href="https://www.insidehighered.com/admissions/article/2018/06/15/university-chicago-drops-satact-requirement" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             Chicago Drops SAT/ACT Requirement. Will Others Follow?
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
          <p>
          </p>
          <p>

         <h3>
          <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/06/the-top-five-new-tax-papers-2.html">
           <strong>
            The Top Five New Tax Papers
           </strong>
          </a>
         </h3>
         <div class="line">
          <p class="author">
           By
           <a href="#">
            Paul Caron
           </a>
          </p>
          <div class="share hidden-phone">
           <a href="#">

         <div class="hidden-phone">
          <p style="text-align: justify;">
           <a class="asset-img-link" href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef0224df35d031200b-popup" onclick="window.open( this.href, '_blank', 'width=640,height=480,scrollbars=no,resizable=no,toolbar=no,directories=no,location=no,menubar=no,status=no,left=0,top=0' ); return false" style="float: right;">
            <img alt="SSRN Logo (2018)" class="asset asset-image at-xid-6a00d8341c4eab53ef0224df35d031200b img-responsive" src="http://taxprof.typepad.com/.a/6a00d8341c4eab53ef0224df35d031200b-300wi" style="width: 300px; margin: 0px 0px 5px 5px;" title="SSRN Logo (2018)"/>
           </a>
           This week's list of the
           <a href="http://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/topten/topTenResults.cfm?groupingId=305496&amp;netorjrnl=ntwk">
            Top 5 Recent Tax Paper Downloads
           </a>
           is the same as last week's list, with some reshuffling of the order of the papers within the Top 5:
          </p>
          <ol>
           <li>
            [290 Downloads]
            <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/04/graetz-the-2017-tax-cuts-how-polarized-politics-produced-precarious-policy.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             The 2017 Tax Cuts: How Polarized Politics Produced Precarious Policy
            </a>
            , by Michael Graetz (Columbia)
           </li>
           <li>
            [244 Downloads]
            <a href="https://papers.ssrn.com/sol3/papers.cfm?abstract_id=3165592" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             IRC Section 678 and the Beneficiary Deemed Owner Trust (BDOT)
            </a>
            , by Edwin Morrow
           </li>
           <li>
            [236 Downloads]
            <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/05/sanchirico-the-new-us-tax-preference-for-foreign-derived-intangible-income.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             The New U.S. Tax Preference for 'Foreign-Derived Intangible Income'
            </a>
            , by Chris Sanchirico (Pennsylvania)
           </li>
           <li>
            [223 Downloads]
            <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/05/manns-todd-section-529-plans-are-not-the-ideal-college-savings-vehicle-for-most-families.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             Higher Education Savings and Planning: Tax and Nontax Considerations
            </a>
            , by Philip Manns (Liberty) &amp; Timothy Todd (Liberty)
           </li>
           <li>
            [185 Downloads]
            <a href="http://taxprof.typepad.com/taxprof_blog/2018/05/borden-like-kind-exchanges-after-the-2017-tax-act.html" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank">
             Code Sec. 1031 after the 2017 Tax Act
            </a>
            , by Brad Borden (Brooklyn)
           </li>
          </ol>
